I've uploaded a code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
formatter: Arrow function body breaks after => when JSDoc type cast is in body
## Input

Found in [sveltejs/svelte](https://github.com/sveltejs/svelte) repo.

Files: `packages/svelte/src/compiler/legacy.js` (20+ instances), `packages/svelte/src/compiler/phases/3-transform/client/visitors/EachBlock.js`, `packages/svelte/src/compiler/phases/3-transform/client/visitors/Program.js`, `packages/svelte/src/compiler/phases/3-transform/server/visitors/Program.js`, `packages/svelte/src/compiler/phases/3-transform/shared/transform-async.js`

Minimal reproduction:

```js
// Example 1: .map() callback
const result = items.map(
  (child) => /** @type {SomeType} */ (visit(child))
);

// Example 2: function argument
const body = transform_body(
  state.analysis.instance_body,
  b.id('$.run'),
  (node) => /** @type {Node} */ (context.visit(node))
);
```

## Config

```jsonc
{
  "useTabs": true,
  "singleQuote": true,
  "trailingComma": "none",
  "printWidth": 100
}
```

## Oxfmt output

```js
// Example 1
const result = items.map((child) =>
	/** @type {SomeType} */ (visit(child))
);

// Example 2
const body = transform_body(state.analysis.instance_body, b.id('$.run'), (node) =>
	/** @type {Node} */ (context.visit(node))
);
```

## Prettier output

Prettier version: `3.8.1`

```js
// Example 1
const result = items.map(
	(child) => /** @type {SomeType} */ (visit(child))
);

// Example 2
const body = transform_body(
	state.analysis.instance_body,
	b.id('$.run'),
	(node) => /** @type {Node} */ (context.visit(node))
);
```

## Additional notes

When an arrow function body starts with a JSDoc inline type cast (`/** @type {X} */`), Prettier breaks after the opening parenthesis and keeps the entire arrow expression on one line, while Oxfmt breaks after `=>` and puts the JSDoc type cast + body on the next line.

This pattern occurs 20+ times in `legacy.js` alone (all with the same `.map((child) => /** @type {X} */ (visit(child)))` pattern), plus several other files. It's the most frequent diff in the Svelte repo.

</pr_description>

    92	    }
    93	
    94	    #[inline]
    95	    pub fn format(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
    96	        let layout = ArrowFunctionLayout::for_arrow(self.arrow, self.options);
    97	
    98	        match layout {
    99	            ArrowFunctionLayout::Chain(chain) => {
   100	                write!(f, chain);
   101	            }
   102	            ArrowFunctionLayout::Single(arrow) => {
   103	                let body = &arrow.body();
   104	
   105	                let formatted_signature = format_with(|f| {
   106	                    write!(
   107	                        f,
   108	                        [
   109	                            format_signature(
   110	                                arrow,
   111	                                self.options.call_argument_layout.is_some(),
   112	                                true,
   113	                                self.options.cache_mode
   114	                            ),
   115	                            space(),
   116	                            "=>"
   117	                        ]
   118	                    );
   119	                });
   120	
   121	                let format_body = FormatMaybeCachedFunctionBody {
   122	                    body,
   123	                    expression: arrow.expression(),
   124	                    mode: self.options.cache_mode,
   125	                };
   126	
   127	                // With arrays, arrow self and objects, they have a natural line breaking strategy:
   128	                // Arrays and objects become blocks:
   129	                //
   130	                //    [
   131	                //      100000,
   132	                //      200000,
   133	                //      300000
   134	                //    ]
   135	                //
   136	                // Arrow self get line broken after the `=>`:
   137	                //
   138	                //  (foo) => (bar) =>
   139	                //     (foo + bar) * (foo + bar)
   140	                //
   141	                // Therefore if our body is an arrow self, array, or object, we
   142	                // do not have a soft line break after the arrow because the body is
   143	                // going to get broken anyways.
   144	                let arrow_expression = arrow.get_expression();
   145	
   146	                if let Some(Expression::SequenceExpression(sequence)) = arrow_expression {
   147	                    return if let Some(format_sequence) =
   148	                        format_sequence_with_leading_comment(sequence.span(), &format_body, f)
   149	                    {
   150	                        write!(f, [group(&format_args!(formatted_signature, format_sequence))]);
   151	                    } else {
   152	                        write!(
   153	                            f,
   154	                            [group(&format_args!(
   155	                                formatted_signature,
   156	                                group(&format_args!(
   157	                                    space(),
   158	                                    token("("),
   159	                                    soft_block_indent(&format_body),
   160	                                    token(")")
   161	                                ))
   162	                            ))]
   163	                        );
   164	                    };
   165	                }
   166	
   167	                write!(f, formatted_signature);
   168	
   169	                let body_has_soft_line_break =
   170	                    arrow_expression.is_none_or(|expression| match expression {
   171	                        Expression::ArrowFunctionExpression(_)
   172	                        | Expression::ArrayExpression(_)
   173	                        | Expression::ObjectExpression(_) => {
   174	                            !f.comments().has_leading_own_line_comment(body.span().start)
   175	                        }
   176	                        Expression::JSXElement(_) | Expression::JSXFragment(_) => true,
   177	                        _ => {
   178	                            is_multiline_template_starting_on_same_line(expression, f.source_text())
   179	                                || is_huggable_html_embed(expression, f)
   180	                        }
   181	                    });
   182	
   183	                if body_has_soft_line_break {
   184	                    write!(f, [space(), format_body]);
   185	                } else {
   186	                    let should_add_parens = arrow.expression && should_add_parens(body);
   187	
   188	                    let is_last_call_arg = matches!(
   189	                        self.options.call_argument_layout,
   190	                        Some(GroupedCallArgumentLayout::GroupedLastArgument)
   191	                    );
   192	
   193	                    let should_add_soft_line = is_last_call_arg
   194	                        // if it's inside a JSXExpression (e.g. an attribute) we should align the expression's closing } with the line with the opening {.
   195	                        || (matches!(self.arrow.parent(), AstNodes::JSXExpressionContainer(container)
   196	                            if !f.context().comments().has_comment_in_range(arrow.span.end, container.span.end)));
   197	
   198	                    write!(
   199	                        f,
   200	                        group(&format_args!(
   201	                            soft_line_indent_or_space(&format_with(|f| {
   202	                                if should_add_parens {
   203	                                    write!(f, if_group_fits_on_line(&"("));
   204	                                }
   205	
   206	                                write!(f, format_body);
   207	
   208	                                if should_add_parens {
   209	                                    write!(f, if_group_fits_on_line(&")"));
   210	                                }
   211	                            })),
   212	                            is_last_call_arg.then_some(&FormatTrailingCommas::All),
   213	                            should_add_soft_line.then_some(soft_line_break())
   214	                        ))
   215	                    );
   216	                }
   217	            }
   218	        }
   219	    }
   220	}

   228	enum ArrowFunctionLayout<'a, 'b> {
   229	    /// Arrow function with a non-arrow function body
   230	    Single(&'b AstNode<'a, ArrowFunctionExpression<'a>>),
   231	
   232	    /// A chain of at least two arrow functions.
   233	    ///
   234	    /// An arrow function is part of the chain when it is the body of the parent arrow function.
   235	    ///
   236	    /// The idea of arrow chains is that they break after the `=>` token
   237	    ///
   238	    /// ```javascript
   239	    /// const x =
   240	    ///   (a): string =>
   241	    ///   (b) =>
   242	    ///   (c) =>
   243	    ///   (d) =>
   244	    ///   (e) =>
   245	    ///     f;
   246	    /// ```
   247	    Chain(ArrowChain<'a, 'b>),
   248	}
   249	
   250	impl<'a, 'b> ArrowFunctionLayout<'a, 'b> {
   251	    /// Determines the layout for the passed arrow function. See [ArrowFunctionLayout] for a description
   252	    /// of the different layouts.
   253	    fn for_arrow(
   254	        arrow: &'b AstNode<'a, ArrowFunctionExpression<'a>>,
   255	        options: FormatJsArrowFunctionExpressionOptions,
   256	    ) -> ArrowFunctionLayout<'a, 'b> {
   257	        let mut head = None;
   258	        let mut middle = Vec::new();
   259	        let mut current = arrow;
   260	        let mut should_break = false;

   261	        let is_non_grouped_or_grouped_last_argument = matches!(
   262	            options.call_argument_layout,
   263	            None | Some(GroupedCallArgumentLayout::GroupedLastArgument)
   264	        );
   265	
   266	        loop {
   267	            if is_non_grouped_or_grouped_last_argument
   268	                && current.expression()
   269	                && let Some(AstNodes::ExpressionStatement(expr_stmt)) =
   270	                    current.body().statements().first().map(AstNode::<Statement>::as_ast_nodes)
   271	                && let AstNodes::ArrowFunctionExpression(next) =
   272	                    &expr_stmt.expression().as_ast_nodes()
   273	            {
   274	                should_break = should_break || Self::should_break_chain(current);
   275	
   276	                should_break = should_break || Self::should_break_chain(next);
   277	
   278	                if head.is_none() {
   279	                    head = Some(current);
   280	                } else {
   281	                    middle.push(current);
   282	                }
   283	
   284	                current = next;
   285	                continue;
   286	            }
   287	            break match head {
   288	                None => ArrowFunctionLayout::Single(current),
   289	                Some(head) => ArrowFunctionLayout::Chain(ArrowChain {
   290	                    head,
   291	                    middle,
   292	                    tail: current,
   293	                    expand_signatures: should_break,
   294	                    options,
   295	                }),
   296	            };
   297	        }
   298	    }
   299	
   300	    /// Returns a `true` result if the arrow function contains any elements which
   301	    /// should force the chain to break onto multiple lines. This includes any kind
   302	    /// of return type annotation if the function also takes parameters (e.g.,
   303	    /// `(a, b): bool => ...`), any kind of rest/object/array binding parameter
   304	    /// (e.g., `({a, b: foo}) => ...`), and any kind of initializer for a parameter
   305	    /// (e.g., `(a = 2) => ...`).
   306	    ///
   307	    /// The complexity of these expressions limits their legibility when printed
   308	    /// inline, so they force the chain to break to preserve clarity. Any other
   309	    /// cases are considered simple enough to print in a single line.
   310	    fn should_break_chain(arrow: &ArrowFunctionExpression<'a>) -> bool {
   311	        if arrow.type_parameters.is_some() {
   312	            return true;
   313	        }
   314	
   315	        let parameters = &arrow.params;
   316	
   317	        // This matches Prettier, which allows type annotations when
   318	        // grouping arrow expressions, but disallows them when grouping
   319	        // normal function expressions.
   320	        if !has_only_simple_parameters(parameters, true) {
   321	            return true;
   322	        }
   323	
   324	        let has_parameters = !parameters.items.is_empty();
   325	        let has_type_and_parameters = arrow.return_type.is_some() && has_parameters;
   326	        has_type_and_parameters || has_rest_object_or_array_parameter(parameters)
   327	    }
   328	}
   329	
   330	/// Returns `true` for a template that starts on the same line as the previous token and contains a line break.
   331	///
   332	///
   333	/// # Examples
   334	///
   335	/// ```javascript
   336	/// "test" + `
   337	///   some content
   338	/// `;
   339	/// ```
   340	///
   341	/// Returns `true` because the template starts on the same line as the `+` token and its text contains a line break.
   342	///
   343	/// ```javascript
   344	/// "test" + `no line break`
   345	/// ```
   346	///
   347	/// Returns `false` because the template text contains no line break.
   348	///
   349	/// ```javascript
   350	/// "test" +
   351	///     `template
   352	///     with line break`;
   353	/// ```
   354	///
   355	/// Returns `false` because the template isn't on the same line as the '+' token.
   356	pub fn is_multiline_template_starting_on_same_line(
   357	    expression: &Expression,
   358	    source_text: SourceText,
   359	) -> bool {
   360	    let (start, template) = match expression {
   361	        Expression::TemplateLiteral(template) => (template.span.start, template.as_ref()),
   362	        Expression::TaggedTemplateExpression(tagged) => (tagged.span.start, &tagged.quasi),
   363	        _ => return false,
   364	    };
   365	
   366	    template.quasis.iter().any(|quasi| source_text.contains_newline(quasi.span))
   367	        && !source_text.has_newline_before(start)
   368	}
   369	
   370	/// Returns `true` if the expression is an HTML embed template that should be hugged.
   371	///
   372	/// This covers both ``html`...` `` tagged templates and ``/* HTML */ `...` `` comment-annotated templates.
   373	/// It is needed when the source is single-line but HTML formatting introduces line breaks.
   374	/// Without this, `ExpandParent` emitted by the HTML formatter causes `will_break()` to return `true`,
   375	/// expanding the surrounding construct instead of hugging.
   376	///
   377	/// Prettier hugs HTML embed templates when the content has leading AND trailing whitespace,
   378	/// or when `htmlWhitespaceSensitivity` is `"ignore"`.
   379	/// In these cases, the template stays on the same line as the parent construct:
   380	/// - Call arguments: ``foo(html`<div>...</div>`)``
   381	/// - Arrow function body: ``const a = (b) => html`<div>...</div>` ``
   382	///
   383	/// When there is no leading+trailing whitespace,
   384	/// `hug: false` is set and the template is expanded (not hugged).
   385	///
   386	/// Prettier achieves this via `label({ embed: true, hug })` + `shouldExpandLastArg`.
   387	/// We replicate it by detecting the same conditions on the expression.
   388	pub fn is_huggable_html_embed(expression: &Expression<'_>, f: &Formatter<'_, '_>) -> bool {
   389	    let template = match expression {
   390	        Expression::TaggedTemplateExpression(tagged) => {
   391	            if !matches!(&tagged.tag, Expression::Identifier(id) if id.name.as_str() == "html") {
   392	                return false;
   393	            }
   394	            // Exclude cases where a line comment between tag and quasi forces a line break
   395	            // e.g., ``html // oops \n`...` ``
   396	            if f.source_text()
   397	                .contains_newline_between(tagged.tag.span().end, tagged.quasi.span.start)
   398	            {
   399	                return false;
   400	            }
   401	            &tagged.quasi
   402	        }
   403	        Expression::TemplateLiteral(template) => {
   404	            // Check for `/* HTML */` leading comment
   405	            let comments = f.comments().comments_before(template.span.start);
   406	            if !comments.last().is_some_and(|comment| {
   407	                comment.is_block() && f.source_text().text_for(&comment.content_span()) == " HTML "
   408	            }) {
   409	                return false;
   410	            }
   411	            template.as_ref()
   412	        }
   413	        _ => return false,
   414	    };
   415	
   416	    // Always hug when htmlWhitespaceSensitivity is "ignore"
   417	    if f.options().html_whitespace_sensitivity_ignore {
   418	        return true;
   419	    }
   420	
   421	    // Hug when the cooked content has both leading and trailing whitespace
   422	    let has_leading_ws = template
   423	        .quasis
   424	        .first()
   425	        .and_then(|q| q.value.cooked.as_ref())
   426	        .is_some_and(|s| s.starts_with(|c: char| c.is_ascii_whitespace()));
   427	    let has_trailing_ws = template
   428	        .quasis
   429	        .last()
   430	        .and_then(|q| q.value.cooked.as_ref())
   431	        .is_some_and(|s| s.ends_with(|c: char| c.is_ascii_whitespace()));
   432	    has_leading_ws && has_trailing_ws
   433	}
   434	
   435	struct ArrowChain<'a, 'b> {
   436	    /// The top most arrow function in the chain
   437	    head: &'b AstNode<'a, ArrowFunctionExpression<'a>>,
   438	
   439	    /// The arrow functions in the chain that are neither the first nor the last.
   440	    /// Empty for chains consisting only of two arrow functions.
   441	    middle: Vec<&'b AstNode<'a, ArrowFunctionExpression<'a>>>,
   442	
   443	    /// The last arrow function in the chain
   444	    tail: &'b AstNode<'a, ArrowFunctionExpression<'a>>,
   445	
   446	    options: FormatJsArrowFunctionExpressionOptions,
   447	
   448	    /// Whether the group wrapping the signatures should be expanded or not.
   449	    expand_signatures: bool,
   450	}
   451	
   452	impl<'a, 'b> ArrowChain<'a, 'b> {
   453	    /// Returns an iterator over all arrow functions in this chain
   454	    fn arrows(&self) -> impl Iterator<Item = &'b AstNode<'a, ArrowFunctionExpression<'a>>> {
   455	        use std::iter::once;
   456	        once(self.head).chain(self.middle.iter().copied()).chain(once(self.tail))
   457	    }
   458	}
   459	
   460	impl<'a> Format<'a> for ArrowChain<'a, '_> {
   461	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
   462	        let ArrowChain { tail, expand_signatures, .. } = *self;
   463	
   464	        let tail_body = tail.body();
   465	        let is_grouped_call_arg_layout = self.options.call_argument_layout.is_some();
   466	
   467	        // If this chain is the callee in a parent call expression, then we
   468	        // want it to break onto a new line to clearly show that the arrow
   469	        // chain is distinct and the _result_ is what's being called.
   470	        // Example:
   471	        //      (() => () => a)()
   472	        // becomes
   473	        //      (
   474	        //        () => () =>
   475	        //          a
   476	        //      )();
   477	        let is_callee = self.head.is_call_like_callee();
   478	
   479	        // With arrays, objects, sequence expressions, and block function bodies,
   480	        // the opening brace gives a convenient boundary to insert a line break,
   481	        // allowing that token to live immediately after the last arrow token
   482	        // and save a line from being printed with just the punctuation.
   483	        //
   484	        // (foo) => (bar) => [a, b]
   485	        //
   486	        // (foo) => (bar) => [
   487	        //   a,
   488	        //   b
   489	        // ]
   490	        //
   491	        // If the body is _not_ one of those kinds, then we'll want to insert a
   492	        // soft line break before the body so that it prints on a separate line
   493	        // in its entirety.
   494	        let body_on_separate_line = !tail.get_expression().is_none_or(|expression| {
   495	            matches!(
   496	                expression,
   497	                Expression::ObjectExpression(_)
   498	                    | Expression::ArrayExpression(_)
   499	                    | Expression::SequenceExpression(_)
   500	                    | Expression::JSXElement(_)
   501	                    | Expression::JSXFragment(_)
   502	            )
   503	        });
   504	
   505	        // If the arrow chain will break onto multiple lines, either because
   506	        // it's a callee or because the body is printed on its own line, then
   507	        // the signatures should be expanded first.
   508	        let break_signatures = (is_callee && body_on_separate_line)
   509	            || matches!(
   510	                self.options.assignment_layout,
   511	                Some(AssignmentLikeLayout::ChainTailArrowFunction)
   512	            );
   513	
   514	        // Arrow chains as callees or as the right side of an assignment
   515	        // indent the entire signature chain a single level and do _not_
   516	        // indent a second level for additional signatures after the first:
   517	        //   const foo =
   518	        //     (a) =>
   519	        //     (b) =>
   520	        //     (c) =>
   521	        //       0;
   522	        // This tracks that state and is used to prevent the insertion of
   523	        // additional indents under `format_arrow_signatures`, then also to
   524	        // add the outer indent under `format_inner`.
   525	        let has_initial_indent = is_callee
   526	            || self
   527	                .options
   528	                .assignment_layout
   529	                .is_some_and(|layout| layout != AssignmentLikeLayout::BreakAfterOperator);
   530	
   531	        let format_arrow_signatures = format_with(|f| {
   532	            let join_signatures = format_with(|f| {
   533	                let mut is_first_in_chain = true;
   534	                for arrow in self.arrows() {
   535	                    // The first comment in the chain gets formatted by the
   536	                    // parent (the FormatJsArrowFunctionExpression), but the
   537	                    // rest of the arrows in the chain need to format their
   538	                    // comments manually, since they won't have their own
   539	                    // Format node to handle it.
   540	                    let should_format_comments = !is_first_in_chain
   541	                        && f.context().comments().has_comment_before(arrow.span.start);
   542	                    let is_first = is_first_in_chain;
   543	
   544	                    let formatted_signature = format_with(|f| {
   545	                        let format_leading_comments = format_with(|f| {
   546	                            if should_format_comments {
   547	                                // A grouped layout implies that the arrow chain is trying to be rendered
   548	                                // in a condensed, single-line format (at least the signatures, not
   549	                                // necessarily the body). In that case, we _need_ to prevent the leading
   550	                                // comments from inserting line breaks. But if it's _not_ a grouped layout,
   551	                                // then we want to _force_ the line break so that the leading comments
   552	                                // don't inadvertently end up on the previous line after the fat arrow.
   553	                                if is_grouped_call_arg_layout {
   554	                                    write!(f, [space(), format_leading_comments(arrow.span())]);
   555	                                } else {
   556	                                    write!(
   557	                                        f,
   558	                                        [
   559	                                            soft_line_break_or_space(),
   560	                                            format_leading_comments(arrow.span())
   561	                                        ]
   562	                                    );
   563	                                }
   564	                            }
   565	                        });
   566	
   567	                        let start = arrow.span().start;
   568	                        write!(
   569	                            f,
   570	                            [
   571	                                FormatContentWithCacheMode::new(
   572	                                    Span::new(start, start),
   573	                                    format_leading_comments,
   574	                                    self.options.cache_mode,
   575	                                ),
   576	                                format_signature(
   577	                                    arrow,
   578	                                    is_grouped_call_arg_layout,
   579	                                    is_first,
   580	                                    self.options.cache_mode
   581	                                )
   582	                            ]
   583	                        );
   584	                    });
   585	
   586	                    // Arrow chains indent a second level for every item other than the first:
   587	                    //   (a) =>
   588	                    //     (b) =>
   589	                    //     (c) =>
   590	                    //       0
   591	                    // Because the chain is printed as a flat list, each entry needs to set
   592	                    // its own indention. This ensures that the first item keeps the same
   593	                    // level as the surrounding content, and then each subsequent item has
   594	                    // one additional level, as shown above.
   595	                    if is_first_in_chain || has_initial_indent {
   596	                        is_first_in_chain = false;
   597	                        write!(f, [formatted_signature]);
   598	                    } else {
   599	                        write!(f, [indent(&formatted_signature)]);
   600	                    }
   601	
   602	                    // The arrow of the tail is formatted outside of the group to ensure it never
   603	                    // breaks from the body
   604	                    if !std::ptr::eq(arrow, tail) {
   605	                        write!(f, [space(), "=>"]);
   606	                    }
   607	                }
   608	            });
   609	
   610	            group(&join_signatures).should_expand(expand_signatures).fmt(f);
   611	        });
   612	
   613	        let format_tail_body_inner = format_with(|f| {
   614	            let format_tail_body = FormatMaybeCachedFunctionBody {
   615	                body: tail_body,
   616	                expression: tail.expression(),
   617	                mode: self.options.cache_mode,
   618	            };
   619	
   620	            // Ensure that the parens of sequence expressions end up on their own line if the

   708	fn should_add_parens(body: &AstNode<'_, FunctionBody<'_>>) -> bool {
   709	    let AstNodes::ExpressionStatement(stmt) = body.statements().first().unwrap().as_ast_nodes()
   710	    else {
   711	        unreachable!()
   712	    };
   713	
   714	    // Add parentheses to avoid confusion between `a => b ? c : d` and `a <= b ? c : d`
   715	    // but only if the body isn't an object/function or class expression because parentheses are always required in that
   716	    // case and added by the object expression itself
   717	    if matches!(&stmt.expression, Expression::ConditionalExpression(_)) {
   718	        !matches!(
   719	            ExpressionLeftSide::leftmost(stmt.expression()).as_ref(),
   720	            Expression::ObjectExpression(_)
   721	                | Expression::FunctionExpression(_)
   722	                | Expression::ClassExpression(_)
   723	        )
   724	    } else {
   725	        false
   726	    }
   727	}
   728	
   729	fn has_rest_object_or_array_parameter(params: &FormalParameters) -> bool {
   730	    params.rest.is_some()
   731	        || params.items.iter().any(|param| param.pattern.is_destructuring_pattern())
   732	}
   733	
   734	/// Writes the arrow function type parameters, parameters, and return type annotation.
   735	///
   736	/// Formats the parameters and return type annotation without any soft line breaks if `is_grouped_call_argument` is `true`
   737	/// so that the parameters and return type are kept on the same line.
   738	fn format_signature<'a, 'b>(
   739	    arrow: &'b AstNode<'a, ArrowFunctionExpression<'a>>,
   740	    is_grouped_call_argument: bool,
   741	    is_first_in_chain: bool,
   742	    cache_mode: FunctionCacheMode,
   743	) -> impl Format<'a> + 'b {
   744	    format_with(move |f| {
   745	        let content = format_with(|f| {
   746	            group(&format_args!(
   747	                arrow.r#async().then_some("async "),
   748	                arrow.type_parameters(),
   749	                arrow.params(),
   750	                arrow.return_type().map(FormatNodeWithoutTrailingComments),
   751	            ))
   752	            .fmt(f);
   753	        });
   754	        let format_head = FormatContentWithCacheMode::new(arrow.params.span, content, cache_mode);
   755	
   756	        if is_grouped_call_argument {
   757	            // The first arrow's soft lines have already been removed in the CallArguments.
   758	            if is_first_in_chain {
   759	                write!(f, format_head);
   760	            } else {
   761	                write!(f, [space()]);
   762	                let mut buffer = RemoveSoftLinesBuffer::new(f);
   763	                write!(buffer, format_head);
   764	            }
   765	        } else {
   766	            write!(
   767	                f,
   768	                [
   769	                    // This soft break is placed outside of the group to ensure
   770	                    // that the parameter group only tries to write on a single
   771	                    // line and can't break pre-emptively without also causing
   772	                    // the parent (i.e., this ArrowChain) to break first.
   773	                    (!is_first_in_chain).then_some(soft_line_break_or_space()),
   774	                    format_head
   775	                ]
   776	            );
   777	        }
   778	
   779	        // Print comments before the fat arrow (`=>`)
   780	        let comments_before_fat_arrow =
   781	            f.context().comments().comments_before_character(arrow.params.span().end, b'=');
   782	        let content = FormatTrailingComments::Comments(comments_before_fat_arrow);
   783	        write!(f, [FormatContentWithCacheMode::new(arrow.span, content, cache_mode)]);
   784	    })
   785	}
   786	
   787	/// Formats a function body with additional caching depending on [`mode`](Self::mode).
   788	pub struct FormatMaybeCachedFunctionBody<'a, 'b> {
   789	    /// The body to format.
   790	    pub body: &'b AstNode<'a, FunctionBody<'a>>,
   791	
   792	    /// Is the function body an arrow expression? i.e. `() => expr` instead of `() => {}`
   793	    pub expression: bool,
   794	
   795	    /// If the body should be cached or if the formatter should try to retrieve it from the cache.
   796	    pub mode: FunctionCacheMode,
   797	}
   798	
   799	impl<'a> Format<'a> for FormatMaybeCachedFunctionBody<'a, '_> {
   800	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
   801	        let content = format_with(|f| {
   802	            if self.expression
   803	                && let AstNodes::ExpressionStatement(s) =
   804	                    &self.body.statements().first().unwrap().as_ast_nodes()
   805	            {
   806	                return s.expression().fmt(f);
   807	            }
   808	            self.body.fmt(f);
   809	        });
   810	        FormatContentWithCacheMode::new(self.body.span, content, self.mode).fmt(f);
   811	    }
   812	}
   813	
   814	/// Format a sequence expression in an arrow function body that has a leading comment.
   815	///
   816	/// When an arrow function body is a sequence expression (e.g., `() => (a, b, c)`) and has
   817	/// a leading comment, special formatting is needed to place the comment correctly:
   818	///
   819	/// ```js
   820	/// const f = () =>
   821	///   // comment
   822	///   (a, b, c);
   823	/// ```
   824	///
   825	/// Returns `Some(formatter)` if the sequence has a leading comment, `None` otherwise.
   826	/// When `None`, the caller should use normal formatting with `soft_block_indent`.
   827	///
   828	/// Handles `oxfmt-ignore` by preserving original source text when suppressed.
   829	fn format_sequence_with_leading_comment<'a, 'b>(
   830	    sequence_span: Span,
   831	    format_body: &'b impl Format<'a>,
   832	    f: &Formatter<'_, 'a>,
   833	) -> Option<impl Format<'a> + 'b> {
   834	    if !f.comments().has_comment_before(sequence_span.start) {
   835	        return None;
   836	    }
   837	
   838	    let is_suppressed = f.comments().is_suppressed(sequence_span.start);
   839	
   840	    let format_sequence = format_with(move |f| {
   841	        write!(f, [format_leading_comments(sequence_span), "("]);
   842	        if is_suppressed {
   843	            write!(f, FormatSuppressedNode(sequence_span));
   844	        } else {
   845	            write!(f, format_body);
   846	        }
   847	        write!(f, [")"]);
   848	    });
   849	
   850	    Some(format_with(move |f| {
   851	        write!(f, group(&indent(&format_args!(hard_line_break(), format_sequence))));
   852	    }))
   853	}
   854

     2	use oxc_span::GetSpan;
     3	
     4	use crate::{
     5	    Buffer, Format, format_args,
     6	    formatter::{Formatter, prelude::*, trivia::FormatLeadingComments},
     7	    write,
     8	};
     9	
    10	/// Checks if a node is a type cast node and returns the comments to be printed.
    11	///
    12	/// This function detects if a node is part of a TypeScript type cast pattern
    13	/// by checking for JSDoc type cast comments and proper parenthesis structure.
    14	///
    15	/// Returns:
    16	/// - `Some(&[])` if the node is a type cast node but no comments need to be printed
    17	/// - `Some(&[Comment, ...])` if the node is a type cast node with comments to print
    18	/// - `None` if the node is not a type cast node
    19	pub fn is_type_cast_node<'a>(node: &impl GetSpan, f: &Formatter<'_, 'a>) -> Option<&'a [Comment]> {
    20	    let comments = f.context().comments();
    21	    let span = node.span();
    22	    let source = f.source_text();
    23	
    24	    // Check if there's a closing parenthesis after the node (possibly after comments)
    25	    if !source.next_non_whitespace_byte_is(span.end, b')') {
    26	        let comments_after_node = comments.comments_after(span.end);
    27	        let mut start = span.end;
    28	        // Skip comments after the node to find the next non-whitespace byte whether it's a `)`
    29	        for comment in comments_after_node {
    30	            if !source.bytes_range(start, comment.span.start).trim_ascii_start().is_empty() {
    31	                break;
    32	            }
    33	            start = comment.span.end;
    34	        }
    35	        // Still not a `)`, return early because it's not a type cast
    36	        if !source.next_non_whitespace_byte_is(start, b')') {
    37	            return None;
    38	        }
    39	    }
    40	
    41	    // Check for type cast comment in printed or unprinted comments
    42	    if !comments.is_handled_type_cast_comment()
    43	        && let Some(last_printed_comment) = comments.printed_comments().last()
    44	        && last_printed_comment.span.end <= span.start
    45	        && source.next_non_whitespace_byte_is(last_printed_comment.span.end, b'(')
    46	        && f.comments().is_type_cast_comment(last_printed_comment)
    47	    {
    48	        // Get the source text from the end of type cast comment to the node span
    49	        let node_source_text = source.bytes_range(last_printed_comment.span.end, span.end);
    50	
    51	        // `(/** @type {Number} */ (bar).zoo)`
    52	        //                         ^^^^
    53	        // Should wrap for `baz` rather than `baz.zoo`
    54	        if has_closed_parentheses(node_source_text) {
    55	            None
    56	        } else {
    57	            // Type cast node, but comment was already printed
    58	            Some(&[])
    59	        }
    60	    } else if let Some(type_cast_comment_index) = comments.get_type_cast_comment_index(span) {
    61	        let comments = f.context().comments().unprinted_comments();
    62	        let type_cast_comment = &comments[type_cast_comment_index];
    63	
    64	        // Get the source text from the end of type cast comment to the node span
    65	        let node_source_text = source.bytes_range(type_cast_comment.span.end, span.end);
    66	
    67	        // `(/** @type {Number} */ (bar).zoo)`
    68	        //                         ^^^^
    69	        // Should wrap for `baz` rather than `baz.zoo`
    70	        if has_closed_parentheses(node_source_text) {
    71	            None
    72	        } else {
    73	            // Type cast node with comments to print
    74	            Some(&comments[..=type_cast_comment_index])
    75	        }
    76	    } else {
    77	        // No typecast comment
    78	        None
    79	    }
    80	}
    81	
    82	/// Formats a node with TypeScript type cast comments if present.
    83	///
    84	/// This function handles the formatting of JSDoc type cast comments that appear
    85	/// immediately before parenthesized expressions, creating patterns like:
    86	/// `(/** @type {string} */ value)` or `(/** @type {number} */ (expression))`
    87	///
    88	/// The function:
    89	/// 1. Checks if there's a closing parenthesis after the node (indicating a type cast)
    90	/// 2. Looks for associated type cast comments that precede the node
    91	/// 3. Wraps the node in parentheses with proper formatting and indentation
    92	/// 4. Handles both object/array expressions and other expression types differently
    93	///
    94	/// Returns `Ok(true)` if the node was formatted as a type cast, `Ok(false)` otherwise.
    95	/// This allows callers to know whether they need to apply their own formatting.
    96	pub fn format_type_cast_comment_node<'a, T>(
    97	    node: &(impl Format<'a, T> + GetSpan),
    98	    is_object_or_array_expression: bool,
    99	    f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>,
   100	) -> bool {
   101	    // Check if this is a type cast node and get the comments to print
   102	    let Some(type_cast_comments) = is_type_cast_node(node, f) else {
   103	        return false;
   104	    };
   105	
   106	    // Print the type cast comments if any
   107	    if !type_cast_comments.is_empty() {
   108	        write!(f, [FormatLeadingComments::Comments(type_cast_comments)]);
   109	    }
   110	
   111	    let span = node.span();
   112	    f.context_mut().comments_mut().mark_as_type_cast_node(node);
   113	
   114	    // https://github.com/prettier/prettier/blob/7584432401a47a26943dd7a9ca9a8e032ead7285/src/language-js/print/estree.js#L117-L120
   115	    if is_object_or_array_expression && !f.comments().has_comment_before(span.start) {
   116	        write!(f, group(&format_args!("(", &format_with(|f| node.fmt(f)), ")")));
   117	    } else {
   118	        write!(f, group(&format_args!("(", soft_block_indent(&format_with(|f| node.fmt(f))), ")")));
   119	    }
   120	
   121	    true
   122	}
   123	
   124	/// Check if the source text has properly closed parentheses starting with '('.
   125	/// Returns true if the text starts with '(' and all parentheses are balanced.
   126	fn has_closed_parentheses(source: &[u8]) -> bool {
   127	    let mut paren_count = 0i32;
   128	    let mut i = 0;
   129	
   130	    while i < source.len() {
   131	        match source[i] {
   132	            b'(' => paren_count += 1,
   133	            b')' => {
   134	                paren_count -= 1;
   135	                if paren_count == 0 {
   136	                    return true;
   137	                }
   138	            }
   139	            b'/' if i + 1 < source.len() => {
   140	                match source[i + 1] {
   141	                    b'/' => {
   142	                        // Skip to end of line comment
   143	                        i += 2;
   144	                        while i < source.len() && source[i] != b'\n' {
   145	                            i += 1;
   146	                        }
   147	                        continue;
   148	                    }
   149	                    b'*' => {
   150	                        // Skip to end of block comment

   305	        let comments = self.unprinted_comments();
   306	        if comments.is_empty() {
   307	            return &[];
   308	        }
   309

   320	            let mut start = preceding_span.end;

   325	                }

/// Tests if a call has multiple anonymous function like (arrow or function expression) arguments.
///
/// ## Examples
///
/// ```javascript
/// compose(sortBy(x => x), flatten, map(x => [x, x*2]));
/// ```
pub fn is_function_composition_args(args: &[Argument<'_>]) -> bool {
    if args.len() <= 1 {
        return false;
    }

    let mut has_seen_function_like = false;
    let is_call_expression_with_arrow_or_function = |call: &CallExpression| {
        call.arguments.iter().any(|arg| {
            matches!(arg, Argument::FunctionExpression(_) | Argument::ArrowFunctionExpression(_))
        })
    };

    for arg in args {
        match arg {
            Argument::FunctionExpression(_) | Argument::ArrowFunctionExpression(_) => {
                if has_seen_function_like {
                    return true;
                }
                has_seen_function_like = true;
            }
            Argument::ChainExpression(chain) => {
                return if let ChainElement::CallExpression(call) = &chain.expression {
                    is_call_expression_with_arrow_or_function(call)
                } else {
                    false
                };
            }
            Argument::CallExpression(call) => {
                if is_call_expression_with_arrow_or_function(call) {
                    return true;
                }
            }
            _ => {}
        }
    }

    false
}

fn format_all_elements_broken_out<'a, 'b>(
    node: &'b AstNode<'a, ArenaVec<'a, Argument<'a>>>,
    elements: impl Iterator<Item = (Option<FormatElement<'a>>, usize)>,
    expand: bool,
    mut buffer: impl Buffer<'a>,
) {
    write!(
        buffer,
        [group(&format_args!(
            "(",
            soft_block_indent(&format_once(move |f| {
                for (index, (element, lines_before)) in elements.into_iter().enumerate() {
                    if let Some(element) = element {
                        if index > 0 {
                            match lines_before {
                                0 | 1 => write!(f, [soft_line_break_or_space()]),
                                _ => write!(f, [empty_line()]),
                            }
                        }

                        f.write_element(element);
                    }
                }

                write!(
                    f,
                    [(!matches!(node.parent(), AstNodes::ImportExpression(_)))
                        .then_some(FormatTrailingCommas::All)]
                );
            })),
            ")",
        ))
        .should_expand(expand)]
    );
}

fn format_all_args_broken_out<'a, 'b>(
    node: &'b AstNode<'a, ArenaVec<'a, Argument<'a>>>,
    expand: bool,
    mut buffer: impl Buffer<'a>,
) {
    let last_index = node.len() - 1;
    write!(
        buffer,
        [group(&format_args!(
            "(",
    }
}

/// Helper for formatting the first grouped argument (see [should_group_first_argument]).
struct FormatGroupedFirstArgument<'a, 'b> {
    argument: &'b AstNode<'a, Argument<'a>>,
}

impl<'a> Format<'a> for FormatGroupedFirstArgument<'a, '_> {
    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
        match self.argument.as_ast_nodes() {
            // Call the arrow function formatting but explicitly passes the call argument layout down
            // so that the arrow function formatting removes any soft line breaks between parameters and the return type.
            AstNodes::ArrowFunctionExpression(arrow) => {
                FormatJsArrowFunctionExpression::new_with_options(
                    arrow,
                    FormatJsArrowFunctionExpressionOptions {
                        cache_mode: FunctionCacheMode::Cache,
                        call_argument_layout: Some(GroupedCallArgumentLayout::GroupedFirstArgument),
                        ..FormatJsArrowFunctionExpressionOptions::default()
                    },
                )
                .fmt(f);
            }

            // For all other nodes, use the normal formatting (which already has been cached)
            _ => self.argument.fmt(f),
        }
    }
}

/// Helper for formatting the last grouped argument (see [should_group_last_argument]).
struct FormatGroupedLastArgument<'a, 'b> {
    /// The argument to format
    argument: &'b AstNode<'a, Argument<'a>>,
    /// Is this the only argument in the arguments list
    is_only: bool,
}

impl<'a> Format<'a> for FormatGroupedLastArgument<'a, '_> {
    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
        // For function and arrow expressions, re-format the node and pass the argument that it is the
        // last grouped argument. This changes the formatting of parameters, type parameters, and return types
        // to remove any soft line breaks.
        match self.argument.as_ast_nodes() {
            AstNodes::Function(function)
                if !self.is_only || function_has_only_simple_parameters(&function.params) =>
            {
                FormatFunction::new_with_options(
                    function,
                    FormatFunctionOptions {
                        cache_mode: FunctionCacheMode::Cache,
                        call_argument_layout: Some(GroupedCallArgumentLayout::GroupedLastArgument),
                    },
                )
                .fmt(f);
            }
            AstNodes::ArrowFunctionExpression(arrow) => {
                FormatJsArrowFunctionExpression::new_with_options(
                    arrow,
                    FormatJsArrowFunctionExpressionOptions {
                        cache_mode: FunctionCacheMode::Cache,
                        call_argument_layout: Some(GroupedCallArgumentLayout::GroupedLastArgument),
                        ..FormatJsArrowFunctionExpressionOptions::default()
                    },
                )
                .fmt(f);
            }
            _ => self.argument.fmt(f),
        }
    }
}

fn function_has_only_simple_parameters(params: &FormalParameters<'_>) -> bool {
    has_only_simple_parameters(params, false)
}

/// Tests if this a simple module import like `import("module-name")` or `require("module-name")`.
pub fn is_simple_module_import(
    arguments: &AstNode<'_, ArenaVec<'_, Argument<'_>>>,
    comments: &Comments,
) -> bool {
    if arguments.len() != 1 {
        return false;
    }

    match arguments.parent() {
        AstNodes::ImportExpression(_) => {}
        AstNodes::CallExpression(call) => {
            match &call.callee {
                Expression::StaticMemberExpression(member) => match member.property.name.as_str() {
                    "resolve" => {
                        match &member.object {
                            Expression::Identifier(ident) if ident.name.as_str() == "require" => {
                                // `require.resolve("foo")`
                            }
                            Expression::MetaProperty(_) => {
                                // `import.meta.resolve("foo")`
                            }
                            _ => return false,
                        }
                    }
                    "paths" => {
                        if !matches!(
                        &member.object, Expression::StaticMemberExpression(member)
                        if matches!(&member.object, Expression::Identifier(ident)
                            if ident.name == "require") && member.property.name.as_str() == "resolve"
                        ) {
                            return false;
                        }
                    }
                    _ => return false,
                },
                _ => {
                    return false;
                }
            }
        }
        _ => return false,
    }

    matches!(arguments.as_ref()[0], Argument::StringLiteral(_))
        && !comments.has_comment_before(arguments.parent().span().end)
}

/// Tests if amd's [`define`](https://github.com/amdjs/amdjs-api/wiki/AMD#define-function-) function.
fn is_commonjs_or_amd_call(
    arguments: &[Argument<'_>],
    call: &AstNode<'_, CallExpression<'_>>,
    f: &Formatter<'_, '_>,
) -> bool {
    let Expression::Identifier(ident) = &call.callee else {
        return false;
    };

    match ident.name.as_str() {
        "require" => {
            let first_argument = &arguments[0];
            if f.comments().has_comment_before(first_argument.span().start) {
                return false;
            }

   284	
   285	pub fn arguments_grouped_layout(
   286	    args: &[Argument],
   287	    f: &Formatter<'_, '_>,
   288	) -> Option<GroupedCallArgumentLayout> {
   289	    // For exactly 2 arguments, we need to check both grouping strategies.
   290	    // To avoid redundant `can_group_expression_argument` calls, we handle this case specially.
   291	    if args.len() == 2 {
   292	        let [first, second] = args else { unreachable!("args.len() == 2 guarantees two elements") };
   293	        let second = second.as_expression()?;
   294	
   295	        // `as_expression()` returns `None` for SpreadElement, which is fine since SpreadElement
   296	        // can never match the last arg's type (used for same-type checking in `should_group_last_argument_impl`).
   297	        let first_expr = first.as_expression();
   298	
   299	        if can_group_expression_argument(second, f) {
   300	            // Check if we should group the last argument (second)
   301	            return should_group_last_argument_impl(2, first_expr, second, f)
   302	                .then_some(GroupedCallArgumentLayout::GroupedLastArgument);
   303	        }
   304	
   305	        // Only check first argument grouping if first is an expression (not SpreadElement)
   306	        should_group_first_argument(first_expr?, second, f)
   307	            .then_some(GroupedCallArgumentLayout::GroupedFirstArgument)
   308	    } else {
   309	        // For other cases (not exactly 2 arguments), only check last argument grouping
   310	        should_group_last_argument(args, f)
   311	            .then_some(GroupedCallArgumentLayout::GroupedLastArgument)
   312	    }
   313	}
   314	
   315	/// Checks if the first argument requires grouping
   316	fn should_group_first_argument(
   317	    first: &Expression,
   318	    second: &Expression,
   319	    f: &Formatter<'_, '_>,
   320	) -> bool {
   321	    match first {
   322	        Expression::FunctionExpression(_) => {}
   323	        // Arrow expressions that are a plain expression or are a chain
   324	        // don't get grouped as the first argument, since they'll either
   325	        // fit entirely on the line or break fully. Only a single arrow
   326	        // with a block body can be grouped to collapse the braces.
   327	        Expression::ArrowFunctionExpression(arrow) => {
   328	            if arrow.expression {
   329	                return false;
   330	            }
   331	        }
   332	        _ => return false,
   333	    }
   334	
   335	    if matches!(
   336	        second,
   337	        Expression::ArrowFunctionExpression(_)
   338	            | Expression::FunctionExpression(_)
   339	            | Expression::ConditionalExpression(_)
   340	    ) {
   341	        return false;
   342	    }
   343	
   344	    let first_span = first.span();
   345	
   346	    // Don't group if there are comments around the first argument:
   347	    // - Before the first argument
   348	    // - After the first argument (next non-whitespace is not a comma)
   349	    // - End-of-line comments between the first and second argument
   350	    if f.comments().has_comment_before(first_span.start)
   351	        || !f.source_text().next_non_whitespace_byte_is(first_span.end, b',')
   352	        || f.comments()
   353	            .comments_in_range(first_span.end, second.span().start)
   354	            .iter()
   355	            .any(|c| c.followed_by_newline())
   356	    {
   357	        return false;
   358	    }
   359	
   360	    is_relatively_short_argument(second)
   361	}
   362	
   363	/// Core logic for checking if the last argument should be grouped.
   364	/// Takes the penultimate argument as an Expression for the 2-argument case,
   365	/// or extracts it from the arguments array for other cases.
   366	fn should_group_last_argument_impl(
   367	    args_len: usize,
   368	    penultimate: Option<&Expression>,
   369	    last: &Expression,
   370	    f: &Formatter<'_, '_>,
   371	) -> bool {
   372	    // Check if penultimate and last are the same type (both Object or both Array)
   373	    if let Some(penultimate) = penultimate
   374	        && matches!(
   375	            (penultimate, last),
   376	            (Expression::ObjectExpression(_), Expression::ObjectExpression(_))
   377	                | (Expression::ArrayExpression(_), Expression::ArrayExpression(_))
   378	                | (Expression::TSAsExpression(_), Expression::TSAsExpression(_))
   379	                | (Expression::TSSatisfiesExpression(_), Expression::TSSatisfiesExpression(_))
   380	                | (Expression::ArrowFunctionExpression(_), Expression::ArrowFunctionExpression(_))
   381	                | (Expression::FunctionExpression(_), Expression::FunctionExpression(_))
   382	        )
   383	    {
   384	        return false;
   385	    }
   386	
   387	    let last_span = last.span();
   388	
   389	    // Don't group if there are comments around the last argument
   390	    let has_comment_before_last = if let Some(penultimate) = penultimate {
   391	        // Check for comments between the penultimate and last argument
   392	        f.comments().comments_in_range(penultimate.span().end, last_span.start).last().is_some_and(
   393	            |c| {
   394	                // Exclude end-of-line comments (treated as previous node's comment)
   395	                // and comments followed by a comma
   396	                !c.followed_by_newline()
   397	                    && !f.source_text().next_non_whitespace_byte_is(c.span.end, b',')
   398	            },
   399	        )
   400	    } else {
   401	        f.comments().has_comment_before(last_span.start)
   402	    };
   403	
   404	    if has_comment_before_last
   405	        // Check for comments after the last argument
   406	        || f.comments().comments_after(last_span.end).first().is_some_and(|c|
   407	        !f.source_text().bytes_contain(last_span.end, c.span.start, b')'))
   408	    {
   409	        return false;
   410	    }
   411	
   412	    match last {
   413	        Expression::ArrayExpression(array) if penultimate.is_some() => {
   414	            // Not for `useEffect`
   415	            if args_len == 2 && matches!(penultimate, Some(Expression::ArrowFunctionExpression(_)))
   416	            {
   417	                return false;
   418	            }
   419	
   420	            !can_concisely_print_array_list(array.span, &array.elements, f)
   421	        }
   422	        _ => true,
   423	    }
   424	}
   425	
   426	/// Checks if the last argument should be grouped.
   427	fn should_group_last_argument(args: &[Argument], f: &Formatter<'_, '_>) -> bool {
   428	    let mut iter = args.iter();
   429	    let Some(last) = iter.next_back().unwrap().as_expression() else {
   430	        return false;
   431	    };
   432	
   433	    let penultimate = iter.next_back().and_then(|arg| arg.as_expression());
   434	
   435	    can_group_expression_argument(last, f)
   436	        && should_group_last_argument_impl(args.len(), penultimate, last, f)
   437	}

   439	/// Check if `ty` is a relatively simple type annotation, allowing a few
   440	/// additional cases through. The simplicity is determined as
   441	/// either being a keyword type or any reference type with no additional type
   442	/// parameters. For example:
   443	/// ```text
   444	///     number          => true
   445	///     unknown         => true
   446	///     HTMLElement     => true
   447	///     string | object => false
   448	///     Foo<string>     => false
   449	/// ```
   450	/// This function also introspects into array and generic types to extract the
   451	/// core type, but only to a limited extent:
   452	/// ```text
   453	///     string[]        => string
   454	///     string[][]      => string
   455	///     string[][][]    => string
   456	///     Foo<string>[][] => string
   457	///     Foo<string[]>[] => string[]
   458	///     Foo<string[][]> => string[][]
   459	/// ```
   460	fn is_simple_ts_type(ty: &TSType<'_>) -> bool {

   544	/// Checks if `argument` benefits from grouping in call arguments.
   545	fn can_group_expression_argument(argument: &Expression<'_>, f: &Formatter<'_, '_>) -> bool {
   546	    match argument {
   547	        Expression::ObjectExpression(object_expression) => {
   548	            !object_expression.properties.is_empty()
   549	                || f.comments().has_comment_in_span(object_expression.span)
   550	        }
   551	        Expression::ArrayExpression(array_expression) => {
   552	            !array_expression.elements.is_empty()
   553	                || f.comments().has_comment_in_span(array_expression.span)
   554	        }
   555	        Expression::TSTypeAssertion(assertion_expression) => {
   556	            can_group_expression_argument(&assertion_expression.expression, f)
   557	        }
   558	        Expression::TSAsExpression(as_expression) => {
   559	            can_group_expression_argument(&as_expression.expression, f)
   560	        }
   561	        Expression::TSSatisfiesExpression(satisfies_expression) => {
   562	            can_group_expression_argument(&satisfies_expression.expression, f)
   563	        }
   564	        Expression::ArrowFunctionExpression(arrow_function) => {
   565	            can_group_arrow_function_expression_argument(arrow_function, false, f)
   566	        }
   567	        Expression::FunctionExpression(_) => true,
   568	        _ => false,
   569	    }
   570	}
   571	
   572	fn can_group_arrow_function_expression_argument(
   573	    arrow_function: &ArrowFunctionExpression,
   574	    is_arrow_recursion: bool,
   575	    f: &Formatter<'_, '_>,
   576	) -> bool {
   577	    let body = &arrow_function.body;
   578	    let return_type_annotation = &arrow_function.return_type;
   579	
   580	    // Handles cases like:
   581	    //
   582	    // app.get("/", (req, res): void => {
   583	    //     res.send("Hello World!");
   584	    // });
   585	    //
   586	    // export class Thing implements OtherThing {
   587	    //   do: (type: Type) => Provider<Prop> = memoize(
   588	    //     (type: ObjectType): Provider<Opts> => {}
   589	    //   );
   590	    // }
   591	    let can_group_type = return_type_annotation.as_ref().is_none_or(|any_type| {
   592	        match &any_type.type_annotation {
   593	            TSType::TSTypeReference(_) => {
   594	                if arrow_function.expression {
   595	                    return false;
   596	                }
   597	                body.statements.iter().any(|statement| match statement {
   598	                    #[expect(clippy::match_same_arms)]
   599	                    Statement::EmptyStatement(_) => {
   600	                        // When the body contains an empty statement, comments in
   601	                        // the body will get attached to that statement rather than
   602	                        // the body itself, so they need to be checked for comments
   603	                        // as well to ensure that the body is still considered
   604	                        // groupable when those empty statements are removed by the
   605	                        // printer.
   606	                        // TODO: it seems no difference if we comment out this line
   607	                        // comments.has_comments(s.span)
   608	                        true
   609	                    }
   610	                    _ => true,
   611	                }) || (body.statements.is_empty() && f.comments().has_comment_before(body.span.end))
   612	            }
   613	            _ => true,
   614	        }
   615	    });
   616	
   617	    if !can_group_type {
   618	        return false;
   619	    }
   620	
   621	    arrow_function.get_expression().is_none_or(|expr| match expr {
   622	        Expression::ObjectExpression(_)
   623	        | Expression::ArrayExpression(_)
   624	        | Expression::JSXElement(_)
   625	        | Expression::JSXFragment(_) => true,
   626	        Expression::ArrowFunctionExpression(inner_arrow_function) => {
   627	            can_group_arrow_function_expression_argument(inner_arrow_function, true, f)
   628	        }
   629	        Expression::ChainExpression(chain) => {
   630	            matches!(chain.expression, ChainElement::CallExpression(_)) && !is_arrow_recursion
   631	        }
   632	        Expression::CallExpression(_) | Expression::ConditionalExpression(_) => !is_arrow_recursion,
   633	        _ => false,
   634	    })
   635	}

   161	/// Formats the trailing comments of `node`.

   163	pub const fn format_trailing_comments<'a>(
   164	    enclosing_span: Span,
   165	    preceding_span: Span,
   166	    following_span_start: u32,
   167	) -> FormatTrailingComments<'a> {
   168	    FormatTrailingComments::Node((enclosing_span, preceding_span, following_span_start))
   169	}
   170	
   171	/// Formats the trailing comments of `node`
   172	#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy)]
   173	pub enum FormatTrailingComments<'a> {
   174	    // (enclosing_span, preceding_span, following_span_start)
   175	    Node((Span, Span, u32)),
   176	    Comments(&'a [Comment]),
   177	}
   178	
   179	impl<'a> Format<'a> for FormatTrailingComments<'a> {
   180	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
   181	        fn format_trailing_comments_impl<'a>(
   182	            comments: impl IntoIterator<Item = &'a Comment>,
   183	            f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>,
   184	        ) {
   185	            let mut total_lines_before = 0;
   186	            let mut previous_comment: Option<&Comment> = None;
   187	
   188	            for comment in comments {
   189	                f.context_mut().comments_mut().increment_printed_count();
   190	
   191	                let lines_before = f.source_text().get_lines_before(comment.span, f.comments());
   192	                total_lines_before += lines_before;
   193	
   194	                let should_nestle = previous_comment.is_some_and(|previous_comment| {
   195	                    should_nestle_adjacent_doc_comments(previous_comment, comment)
   196	                });
   197	
   198	                // This allows comments at the end of nested structures:
   199	                // {
   200	                //   x: 1,
   201	                //   y: 2
   202	                //   // A comment
   203	                // }
   204	                // Those kinds of comments are almost always leading comments, but
   205	                // here it doesn't go "outside" the block and turns it into a
   206	                // trailing comment for `2`. We can simulate the above by checking
   207	                // if this a comment on its own line; normal trailing comments are
   208	                // always at the end of another expression.
   209	                if total_lines_before > 0
   210	                    || previous_comment.is_some_and(|comment| comment.is_line())

    80	/// implements the same behavior: <https://github.com/prettier/prettier/pull/13445/files#diff-3d5eaa2a1593372823589e6e55e7ca905f7c64203ecada0aa4b3b0cdddd5c3ddR160-R178>
    81	fn should_nestle_adjacent_doc_comments(current: &Comment, next: &Comment) -> bool {
    82	    matches!(current.content, CommentContent::Jsdoc)
    83	        && matches!(next.content, CommentContent::Jsdoc)
    84	        && current.is_multiline_block()
    85	        && next.is_multiline_block()
    86	        && current.span.end == next.span.start
    87	}

    89	/// Formats the leading comments of `node`
    90	#[inline]
    91	pub const fn format_leading_comments<'a>(span: Span) -> FormatLeadingComments<'a> {
    92	    FormatLeadingComments::Node(span)
    93	}
    94	
    95	/// Formats the leading comments of a node.
    96	#[derive(Debug, Copy, Clone)]
    97	pub enum FormatLeadingComments<'a> {
    98	    Node(Span),
    99	    Comments(&'a [Comment]),
   100	}
   101	
   102	impl<'a> Format<'a> for FormatLeadingComments<'a> {
   103	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
   104	        fn format_leading_comments_impl<'a>(
   105	            comments: impl IntoIterator<Item = &'a Comment>,
   106	            f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>,
   107	        ) {
   108	            let mut leading_comments_iter = comments.into_iter().peekable();
   109	            while let Some(comment) = leading_comments_iter.next() {
   110	                f.context_mut().comments_mut().increment_printed_count();
   111	                write!(f, comment);
   112	
   113	                match comment.kind {
   114	                    CommentKind::SingleLineBlock | CommentKind::MultiLineBlock => {
   115	                        match f.source_text().lines_after(comment.span.end) {
   116	                            0 => {
   117	                                let should_nestle =
   118	                                    leading_comments_iter.peek().is_some_and(|next_comment| {
   119	                                        should_nestle_adjacent_doc_comments(comment, next_comment)
   120	                                    });
   121	
   122	                                write!(f, [maybe_space(!should_nestle)]);
   123	                            }
   124	                            1 => {
   125	                                if f.source_text().get_lines_before(comment.span, f.comments()) == 0
   126	                                {
   127	                                    write!(f, [soft_line_break_or_space()]);
   128	                                } else {
   129	                                    write!(f, [hard_line_break()]);
   130	                                }
